The album found Carey working predominantly with <a href="/wiki/Jermaine_Dupri" title="Jermaine Dupri">Jermaine Dupri</a>, as well as <a href="/wiki/Bryan-Michael_Cox" title="Bryan-Michael Cox">Bryan-Michael Cox</a>, <a href="/wiki/Manuel_Seal" title="Manuel Seal">Manuel Seal</a>, <a href="/wiki/The_Neptunes" title="The Neptunes">The Neptunes</a> and <a href="/wiki/Kanye_West" title="Kanye West">Kanye West</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-viber_140-0"><a href="#cite_note-viber-140"><span>[</span>140<span>]</span></a></sup> The album debuted atop the charts in several countries, and was warmly accepted by critics. Caroline Sullivan of <i><a href="/wiki/The_Guardian" title="The Guardian">The Guardian</a></i> defined it as "cool, focused and urban [... some of] the first Mariah Carey tunes in years which I wouldn't have to be paid to listen to again",<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-141"><a href="#cite_note-141"><span>[</span>141<span>]</span></a></sup> while <i><a href="/wiki/USA_Today" title="USA Today">USA Today</a></i> '​s Elysa Gardner wrote, "The ballads and midtempo numbers that truly reflect the renewed confidence of a songbird who has taken her shots and kept on flying."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-142"><a href="#cite_note-142"><span>[</span>142<span>]</span></a></sup> The album's second single, "<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/We_Belong_Together_(Mariah_Carey_song)" title="We Belong Together (Mariah Carey song)">We Belong Together</a>", became a "career re-defining"<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-promo_143-0"><a href="#cite_note-promo-143"><span>[</span>143<span>]</span></a></sup> song for Carey, at a point when many critics had considered her career over.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated5_144-0"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated5-144"><span>[</span>144<span>]</span></a></sup> Music critics heralded the song as her "return to form",<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-slanter_145-0"><a href="#cite_note-slanter-145"><span>[</span>145<span>]</span></a></sup> as well as the "return of The Voice",<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-slanter_145-1"><a href="#cite_note-slanter-145"><span>[</span>145<span>]</span></a></sup> while many felt it would revive "faith" in Carey's potential as a <a href="/wiki/Ballad" title="Ballad">balladeer</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-viber_140-1"><a href="#cite_note-viber-140"><span>[</span>140<span>]</span></a></sup> "We Belong Together" broke several records in the United States and became Carey's sixteenth chart topper on the <i><a href="/wiki/Billboard_(magazine)" title="Billboard (magazine)">Billboard</a></i> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hot_100" title="Hot 100">Hot 100</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-records_146-0"><a href="#cite_note-records-146"><span>[</span>146<span>]</span></a></sup> After staying at number one for fourteen non-consecutive weeks, the song became the <a href="/wiki/List_of_Billboard_Hot_100_chart_achievements_and_milestones" title="List of Billboard Hot 100 chart achievements and milestones">second longest running number one song in US chart history</a>, behind Carey's 1996 collaboration with <a href="/wiki/Boyz_II_Men" title="Boyz II Men">Boyz II Men</a>, "<a href="/wiki/One_Sweet_Day" title="One Sweet Day">One Sweet Day</a>".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-records_146-1"><a href="#cite_note-records-146"><span>[</span>146<span>]</span></a></sup> <i>Billboard</i> listed it as the "song of the decade" and the ninth most popular song of all time.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-yahoosales_147-0"><a href="#cite_note-yahoosales-147"><span>[</span>147<span>]</span></a></sup> Besides its chart success, the song broke several airplay records, and according to Nielsen BDS, gathered both the largest one-day and one-week audiences in history.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-148"><a href="#cite_note-148"><span>[</span>148<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>During the week of September 25, 2005, Carey set another record, becoming the first female to occupy the first two spots atop the Hot 100, as "We Belong Together" remained at number one, and her next single, "<a href="/wiki/Shake_It_Off_(Mariah_Carey_song)" title="Shake It Off (Mariah Carey song)">Shake It Off</a>" moved into the number two spot (<a href="/wiki/Ashanti_(singer)" title="Ashanti (singer)">Ashanti</a> had topped the chart in 2002 while being a "featured" singer on the number two single).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-records_146-2"><a href="#cite_note-records-146"><span>[</span>146<span>]</span></a></sup> On the <a href="/wiki/Billboard_Year-End" title="Billboard Year-End">Billboard Hot 100 Year-end Chart</a> of 2005, the song was declared the number one song, a career first for Carey.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-US_yearend_149-0"><a href="#cite_note-US_yearend-149"><span>[</span>149<span>]</span></a></sup> <i>Billboard</i> listed "We Belong Together" ninth on The <a href="/wiki/Billboard_Hot_100_50th_Anniversary_Charts" title="Billboard Hot 100 50th Anniversary Charts">Billboard Hot 100 All-Time Top Songs</a> and was declared the most popular song of the 2000s decade by <i>Billboard</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-decade_150-0"><a href="#cite_note-decade-150"><span>[</span>150<span>]</span></a></sup> The album earned ten <a href="/wiki/Grammy_Award" title="Grammy Award">Grammy Award</a> nominations in 2006–07: eight in 2006 for the original release (the most received by Carey in a single year),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-usaawards_151-0"><a href="#cite_note-usaawards-151"><span>[</span>151<span>]</span></a></sup> and two in 2007 for the <i>Ultra Platinum Edition</i> (from which "<a href="/wiki/Don%27t_Forget_About_Us" title="Don't Forget About Us">Don't Forget About Us</a>" became her seventeenth number-one hit). In 2006 Carey won <a href="/wiki/Grammy_Award_for_Best_Contemporary_R%26B_Album" title="Grammy Award for Best Contemporary R&amp;B Album">Best Contemporary R&amp;B Album</a> for <i>The Emancipation of Mimi</i>, as well as <a href="/wiki/Grammy_Award_for_Best_Female_R%26B_Vocal_Performance" title="Grammy Award for Best Female R&amp;B Vocal Performance">Best Female R&amp;B Vocal Performance</a> and <a href="/wiki/Grammy_Award_for_Best_R%26B_Song" title="Grammy Award for Best R&amp;B Song">Best R&amp;B Song</a> for "We Belong Together".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-usaawards_151-1"><a href="#cite_note-usaawards-151"><span>[</span>151<span>]</span></a></sup> <i>The Emancipation of Mimi</i> was the best-selling album in the United States in 2005, with nearly five million units sold. It was the first album by a solo female artist to become the year's best-selling album since <a href="/wiki/Alanis_Morissette" title="Alanis Morissette">Alanis Morissette</a>'s <i><a href="/wiki/Jagged_Little_Pill" title="Jagged Little Pill">Jagged Little Pill</a></i> in 1996.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-152"><a href="#cite_note-152"><span>[</span>152<span>]</span></a></sup> At the end of 2005, the <a href="/wiki/International_Federation_of_the_Phonographic_Industry" title="International Federation of the Phonographic Industry">IFPI</a> reported that <i>The Emancipation of Mimi</i> had sold more than 7.7 million copies globally, and was the second-best-selling album of the year after <a href="/wiki/Coldplay" title="Coldplay">Coldplay</a>'s <i><a href="/wiki/X%26Y" title="X&amp;Y">X&amp;Y</a></i>. It was the best-selling album worldwide by a solo and female artist.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-world2005_153-0"><a href="#cite_note-world2005-153"><span>[</span>153<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-154"><a href="#cite_note-154"><span>[</span>154<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-155"><a href="#cite_note-155"><span>[</span>155<span>]</span></a></sup> To date, <i>The Emancipation of Mimi</i> has sold over 12 million copies worldwide.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated11_156-0"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated11-156"><span>[</span>156<span>]</span></a></sup> At the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/48th_Grammy_Awards" title="48th Grammy Awards">48th Grammy Awards</a>, Carey performed a medley of "We Belong Together" and "<a href="/wiki/Fly_Like_a_Bird" title="Fly Like a Bird">Fly Like a Bird</a>".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nemn_157-0"><a href="#cite_note-nemn-157"><span>[</span>157<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>In support of the album, Carey embarked on her first headlining tour in three years, named <a href="/wiki/The_Adventures_of_Mimi" title="The Adventures of Mimi">The Adventures of Mimi: The Voice, The Hits, The Tour</a> after a "Carey-centric fan's" music diary.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-158"><a href="#cite_note-158"><span>[</span>158<span>]</span></a></sup> The tour spanned forty stops, with thirty-two in the United States and Canada, two in Africa, and six in Japan.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mtvnews8_159-0"><a href="#cite_note-mtvnews8-159"><span>[</span>159<span>]</span></a></sup> It received warm reaction from music critics and concert goers, many of which celebrated the quality of Carey's live vocals, as well as the show as a whole.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-outshines_160-0"><a href="#cite_note-outshines-160"><span>[</span>160<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-161"><a href="#cite_note-161"><span>[</span>161<span>]</span></a></sup> The tour proved successful, with Carey playing to over 60,000 fans in the two stops in <a href="/wiki/Tunis" title="Tunis">Tunis</a> alone.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sales667_162-0"><a href="#cite_note-sales667-162"><span>[</span>162<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability"><span title="The material near this tag failed verification of its source citation(s). (February 2015)">not in citation given</span></a></i>]</sup> <i><a href="/wiki/The_Adventures_of_Mimi_(video)" title="The Adventures of Mimi (video)">The Adventures of Mimi</a></i> <a href="/wiki/DVD" title="DVD">DVD</a> was released in November 2007 internationally and December 2007 in the US.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2008.E2.80.9309:_E.3DMC.C2.B2_and_Memoirs_of_an_Imperfect_Angel">2008–09: <i>E=MC²</i> and <i>Memoirs of an Imperfect Angel</i></span></h3>
<p>By spring 2007, Carey had begun to work on her eleventh studio album, <i><a href="/wiki/E%3DMC%C2%B2_(Mariah_Carey_album)" title="E=MC² (Mariah Carey album)">E=MC²</a></i>, in a private villa in <a href="/wiki/Anguilla" title="Anguilla">Anguilla</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-163"><a href="#cite_note-163"><span>[</span>163<span>]</span></a></sup> When asked about the album title's meaning, Carey said "<a href="/wiki/Albert_Einstein" title="Albert Einstein">Einstein</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Mass%E2%80%93energy_equivalence" title="Mass–energy equivalence">theory</a>? Physics? <i>Me?</i> Hello! ...Of course I'm poking fun."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-title_164-0"><a href="#cite_note-title-164"><span>[</span>164<span>]</span></a></sup> She characterized it as "<i>Emancipation of Mimi</i> to the second power", and said that she was "freer" on this album than any other.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-title_164-1"><a href="#cite_note-title-164"><span>[</span>164<span>]</span></a></sup> Although <i>E=MC²</i> was well received by most critics,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-165"><a href="#cite_note-165"><span>[</span>165<span>]</span></a></sup> some of them criticized it for being very similar to the formula used on <i>The Emancipation of Mimi</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-angels_166-0"><a href="#cite_note-angels-166"><span>[</span>166<span>]</span></a></sup> Two weeks before the album's release, "<a href="/wiki/Touch_My_Body_(Mariah_Carey_song)" title="Touch My Body (Mariah Carey song)">Touch My Body</a>", the record's lead single, reached the top position on the <i>Billboard</i> Hot 100, becoming Carey's eighteenth number one and making her the solo artist with the <a href="/wiki/List_of_Billboard_Hot_100_chart_achievements_and_milestones#Most_number-one_hits" title="List of Billboard Hot 100 chart achievements and milestones">most number one singles in United States history</a>, pushing her past <a href="/wiki/Elvis_Presley" title="Elvis Presley">Elvis Presley</a> into second place according to the magazine's revised methodology.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-167"><a href="#cite_note-167"><span>[</span>167<span>]</span></a></sup> Carey is second only to <a href="/wiki/The_Beatles" title="The Beatles">The Beatles</a>, who have twenty number-one singles. Additionally, it gave Carey her 79th week atop the Hot 100, tying her with Presley as the artist with the <a href="/wiki/List_of_Billboard_Hot_100_chart_achievements_and_milestones#Most_cumulative_weeks_at_number_one" title="List of Billboard Hot 100 chart achievements and milestones">most weeks at number one in the <i>Billboard</i> chart history</a>."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-168"><a href="#cite_note-168"><span>[</span>168<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Mariah_Carey_2_by_David_Shankbone.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3105" data-file-width="1979" height="267" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/56/Mariah_Carey_2_by_David_Shankbone.jpg/170px-Mariah_Carey_2_by_David_Shankbone.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/56/Mariah_Carey_2_by_David_Shankbone.jpg/255px-Mariah_Carey_2_by_David_Shankbone.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/56/Mariah_Carey_2_by_David_Shankbone.jpg/340px-Mariah_Carey_2_by_David_Shankbone.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Mariah_Carey_2_by_David_Shankbone.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Carey at the 2008 <a href="/wiki/Tribeca_Film_Festival" title="Tribeca Film Festival">Tribeca Film Festival</a>, displaying her engagement ring</div>
</div>
</div>
<p><i>E=MC²</i> debuted at number one on the <i>Billboard</i> 200 with 463,000 copies sold, the biggest opening week sales of her career.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated2_169-0"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated2-169"><span>[</span>169<span>]</span></a></sup> With six number one albums, Carey was tied with <a href="/wiki/Britney_Spears" title="Britney Spears">Britney Spears</a> and <a href="/wiki/Janet_Jackson" title="Janet Jackson">Janet Jackson</a> in the United States for the third most number one albums for a female artist, behind <a href="/wiki/Madonna_(entertainer)" title="Madonna (entertainer)">Madonna</a> with eight and <a href="/wiki/Barbra_Streisand" title="Barbra Streisand">Barbra Streisand</a>'s ten chart toppers.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability"><span title="The material near this tag failed verification of its source citation(s). (February 2015)">not in citation given</span></a></i>]</sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sales_38-1"><a href="#cite_note-sales-38"><span>[</span>38<span>]</span></a></sup> In 2008, <i>Billboard</i> magazine ranked her at number six on the "<a href="/wiki/Billboard_Hot_100_50th_Anniversary_Charts" title="Billboard Hot 100 50th Anniversary Charts">Billboard Hot 100 All-Time Top Artists</a>", making Carey the second most successful female artist in the history of the <i>Billboard</i> Hot 100 chart.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-170"><a href="#cite_note-170"><span>[</span>170<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability"><span title="The material near this tag failed verification of its source citation(s). (February 2015)">not in citation given</span></a></i>]</sup> That year, Carey also played an aspiring singer named Krystal in <i><a href="/wiki/Tennessee_(film)" title="Tennessee (film)">Tennessee</a></i><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-171"><a href="#cite_note-171"><span>[</span>171<span>]</span></a></sup> and had a <a href="/wiki/Cameo_appearance" title="Cameo appearance">cameo appearance</a> in <a href="/wiki/Adam_Sandler" title="Adam Sandler">Adam Sandler</a>'s film <i><a href="/wiki/You_Don%27t_Mess_with_the_Zohan" title="You Don't Mess with the Zohan">You Don't Mess with the Zohan</a></i>, playing herself.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_172-0"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-172"><span>[</span>172<span>]</span></a></sup> Since the album's release, Carey had planned to embark on an extensive tour in support of <i>E=MC²</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mtvvid2_173-0"><a href="#cite_note-mtvvid2-173"><span>[</span>173<span>]</span></a></sup> However, even after a formal announcement, the tour was suddenly cancelled in early December 2008.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-preg_174-0"><a href="#cite_note-preg-174"><span>[</span>174<span>]</span></a></sup> Carey later stated that she had been pregnant during that time period, and suffered a miscarriage, hence she cancelled the tour.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-175"><a href="#cite_note-175"><span>[</span>175<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-derschowitz1_176-0"><a href="#cite_note-derschowitz1-176"><span>[</span>176<span>]</span></a></sup> On January 20, 2009, Carey performed "<a href="/wiki/Hero_(Mariah_Carey_song)" title="Hero (Mariah Carey song)">Hero</a>" at the <a href="/wiki/First_inauguration_of_Barack_Obama" title="First inauguration of Barack Obama">Neighborhood Inaugural Ball</a> after <a href="/wiki/Barack_Obama" title="Barack Obama">Barack Obama</a> was sworn as the first African-American president of the United States.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-177"><a href="#cite_note-177"><span>[</span>177<span>]</span></a></sup> On July 7, 2009, Carey – alongside <a href="/wiki/Trey_Lorenz" title="Trey Lorenz">Trey Lorenz</a> – performed her version of <a href="/wiki/The_Jackson_5" title="The Jackson 5">The Jackson 5</a> song "<a href="/wiki/I%27ll_Be_There_(The_Jackson_5_song)#Mariah_Carey_version" title="I'll Be There (The Jackson 5 song)">I'll Be There</a>" at the memorial service for <a href="/wiki/Michael_Jackson" title="Michael Jackson">Michael Jackson</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-reuters_178-0"><a href="#cite_note-reuters-178"><span>[</span>178<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>In 2009, she appeared as a <a href="/wiki/Social_work" title="Social work">social worker</a> in <i><a href="/wiki/Precious_(film)" title="Precious (film)">Precious</a></i>, the movie adaptation of the 1996 novel <i>Push</i> by <a href="/wiki/Sapphire_(author)" title="Sapphire (author)">Sapphire</a>. The film garnered mostly positive reviews from critics, as had Carey's performance.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-179"><a href="#cite_note-179"><span>[</span>179<span>]</span></a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/Variety_(magazine)" title="Variety (magazine)">Variety</a></i> described her acting as "pitch-perfect".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-180"><a href="#cite_note-180"><span>[</span>180<span>]</span></a></sup> <i>Precious</i> won awards at both the <a href="/wiki/Sundance_Film_Festival" title="Sundance Film Festival">Sundance Film Festival</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Toronto_International_Film_Festival" title="Toronto International Film Festival">Toronto Film Festival</a>, receiving top honors there.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-181"><a href="#cite_note-181"><span>[</span>181<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-182"><a href="#cite_note-182"><span>[</span>182<span>]</span></a></sup> In January 2010, Carey won the Breakthrough Actress Performance Award for her role in <i>Precious</i> at the <a href="/wiki/Palm_Springs_International_Film_Festival" title="Palm Springs International Film Festival">Palm Springs International Film Festival</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Carey_183-0"><a href="#cite_note-Carey-183"><span>[</span>183<span>]</span></a></sup> On September 25, 2009, Carey's twelfth studio album, <i><a href="/wiki/Memoirs_of_an_Imperfect_Angel" title="Memoirs of an Imperfect Angel">Memoirs of an Imperfect Angel</a></i>, was released. Reception for the album was generally positive, but mixed in certain aspects; Stephen Thomas Erlewine of <a href="/wiki/AllMusic" title="AllMusic">AllMusic</a> called it "her most interesting album in a decade",<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-184"><a href="#cite_note-184"><span>[</span>184<span>]</span></a></sup> while Jon Caramanica from <i><a href="/wiki/The_New_York_Times" title="The New York Times">The New York Times</a></i> criticized Carey's vocal performances, decrying her overuse of her softer vocal registers at the expense of her more powerful lower and upper registers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-185"><a href="#cite_note-185"><span>[</span>185<span>]</span></a></sup> Commercially, the album debuted at number three on the <i>Billboard</i> 200, and became the lowest-selling studio album of her career.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-186"><a href="#cite_note-186"><span>[</span>186<span>]</span></a></sup> The album's lead single, "<a href="/wiki/Obsessed_(Mariah_Carey_song)" title="Obsessed (Mariah Carey song)">Obsessed</a>", became her 40th entry on the <i>Billboard</i> Hot 100 and her highest debut on the chart since "<a href="/wiki/My_All" title="My All">My All</a>" in 1998.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-recs_187-0"><a href="#cite_note-recs-187"><span>[</span>187<span>]</span></a></sup> The song debuted at number eleven and peaked at number seven on the chart, and became Carey's 27th US top-ten hit, tying her with <a href="/wiki/Elton_John" title="Elton John">Elton John</a> and <a href="/wiki/Janet_Jackson" title="Janet Jackson">Janet Jackson</a> as the fifth most top-ten hits.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-recs_187-1"><a href="#cite_note-recs-187"><span>[</span>187<span>]</span></a></sup> The album's follow-up single, a cover of <a href="/wiki/Foreigner_(band)" title="Foreigner (band)">Foreigner</a>'s "<a href="/wiki/I_Want_to_Know_What_Love_Is" title="I Want to Know What Love Is">I Want to Know What Love Is</a>", failed to achieve any significant chart success in the United States, or much throughout Europe, but managed to break airplay records in Brazil. The song spent 27 weeks atop the <a href="/wiki/Brasil_Hot_100_Airplay" title="Brasil Hot 100 Airplay">Brasil Hot 100 Airplay</a>, making it the longest running song in the chart's history.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-188"><a href="#cite_note-188"><span>[</span>188<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>On December 31, 2009, Carey embarked her seventh concert tour, <a href="/wiki/Angels_Advocate_Tour" title="Angels Advocate Tour">Angels Advocate Tour</a>, which visited the United States and Canada.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-189"><a href="#cite_note-189"><span>[</span>189<span>]</span></a></sup> Though stateside, the tour spanned few international dates, such as in Brazil and Singapore, where Carey played to over 100,000 spectators. The tour ended on September 26, 2010.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-190"><a href="#cite_note-190"><span>[</span>190<span>]</span></a></sup> On January 30, 2010, it was announced that Carey would release a <a href="/wiki/Remix" title="Remix">remix</a> album of <i>Memoirs of an Imperfect Angel</i>; titled <i>Angels Advocate</i> (an R&amp;B remix album featuring a collection of newly remixed duets with some of Carey's favorite artists).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-reuters_178-1"><a href="#cite_note-reuters-178"><span>[</span>178<span>]</span></a></sup> The album was slated for a March 30, 2010 release, but was eventually cancelled.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-191"><a href="#cite_note-191"><span>[</span>191<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2010.E2.80.9314:_Merry_Christmas_II_You.2C_American_Idol.2C_and_Me._I_Am_Mariah..._The_Elusive_Chanteuse">2010–14: <i>Merry Christmas II You</i>, <i>American Idol</i>, and <i>Me. I Am Mariah... The Elusive Chanteuse</i></span></h3>
<p>Following the cancellation of <i>Angels Advocate</i>, it was announced that Carey would return to the studio to start work on her thirteenth studio album.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-return_192-0"><a href="#cite_note-return-192"><span>[</span>192<span>]</span></a></sup> It was later revealed that it would be her second Christmas album, and follow-up to <i>Merry Christmas</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mimisales2_63-1"><a href="#cite_note-mimisales2-63"><span>[</span>63<span>]</span></a></sup> Longtime collaborators for the project included <a href="/wiki/Jermaine_Dupri" title="Jermaine Dupri">Jermaine Dupri</a>, <a href="/wiki/Johnt%C3%A1_Austin" title="Johntá Austin">Johntá Austin</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bryan-Michael_Cox" title="Bryan-Michael Cox">Bryan-Michael Cox</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Randy_Jackson" title="Randy Jackson">Randy Jackson</a>, as well as new collaborators such as <a href="/wiki/Marc_Shaiman" title="Marc Shaiman">Marc Shaiman</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-aneme_193-0"><a href="#cite_note-aneme-193"><span>[</span>193<span>]</span></a></sup> The release date for the album, titled <i><a href="/wiki/Merry_Christmas_II_You" title="Merry Christmas II You">Merry Christmas II You</a></i>, was November 2, 2010;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-194"><a href="#cite_note-194"><span>[</span>194<span>]</span></a></sup> the track list included six new songs as well as a remix of "<a href="/wiki/All_I_Want_for_Christmas_Is_You" title="All I Want for Christmas Is You">All I Want for Christmas Is You</a>".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-195"><a href="#cite_note-195"><span>[</span>195<span>]</span></a></sup> <i>Merry Christmas II You</i> debuted at number four on the <i>Billboard</i> 200 with sales of 56,000 copies, becoming Carey's 16th top ten album in the United States.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-opening_196-0"><a href="#cite_note-opening-196"><span>[</span>196<span>]</span></a></sup> The album debuted at number one on the <a href="/wiki/Top_R%26B/Hip-Hop_Albums" title="Top R&amp;B/Hip-Hop Albums">R&amp;B/Hip-Hop Albums</a> chart, making it only the second Christmas album to top this chart.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-197"><a href="#cite_note-197"><span>[</span>197<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Mariah_Carey_-_Beautiful_(Live_@_GMA,_May_24,_2013).JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3456" data-file-width="4608" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/18/Mariah_Carey_-_Beautiful_%28Live_%40_GMA%2C_May_24%2C_2013%29.JPG/220px-Mariah_Carey_-_Beautiful_%28Live_%40_GMA%2C_May_24%2C_2013%29.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/18/Mariah_Carey_-_Beautiful_%28Live_%40_GMA%2C_May_24%2C_2013%29.JPG/330px-Mariah_Carey_-_Beautiful_%28Live_%40_GMA%2C_May_24%2C_2013%29.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/18/Mariah_Carey_-_Beautiful_%28Live_%40_GMA%2C_May_24%2C_2013%29.JPG/440px-Mariah_Carey_-_Beautiful_%28Live_%40_GMA%2C_May_24%2C_2013%29.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a>
