</div>
</div>
<p>In May 2010, Carey dropped out of her planned appearance in <i><a href="/wiki/For_Colored_Girls" title="For Colored Girls">For Colored Girls</a></i>, the film adaptation of the play <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/For_Colored_Girls_Who_Have_Considered_Suicide_When_the_Rainbow_Is_Enuf" title="For Colored Girls Who Have Considered Suicide When the Rainbow Is Enuf">For Colored Girls Who Have Considered Suicide When the Rainbow Is Enuf</a></i>, citing medical reasons.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-198"><a href="#cite_note-198"><span>[</span>198<span>]</span></a></sup> In February 2011, Carey announced that she had officially began writing new material for her upcoming fourteenth studio album. Carey recorded a duet with <a href="/wiki/Tony_Bennett" title="Tony Bennett">Tony Bennett</a> for his <i><a href="/wiki/Duets_II_(Tony_Bennett_album)" title="Duets II (Tony Bennett album)">Duets II</a></i> album, titled "When Do The Bells Ring For Me".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-199"><a href="#cite_note-199"><span>[</span>199<span>]</span></a></sup> In October 2011, Carey announced that she re-recorded "All I Want for Christmas Is You" with <a href="/wiki/Justin_Bieber" title="Justin Bieber">Justin Bieber</a> as a duet for his Christmas album, <i><a href="/wiki/Under_the_Mistletoe" title="Under the Mistletoe">Under the Mistletoe</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-200"><a href="#cite_note-200"><span>[</span>200<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-201"><a href="#cite_note-201"><span>[</span>201<span>]</span></a></sup> In November 2011, Carey was included in the remix to the mixtape single "Warning" by <a href="/wiki/Uncle_Murda" title="Uncle Murda">Uncle Murda</a>; the remix also features <a href="/wiki/50_Cent" title="50 Cent">50 Cent</a> and <a href="/wiki/Young_Jeezy" title="Young Jeezy">Young Jeezy</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-202"><a href="#cite_note-202"><span>[</span>202<span>]</span></a></sup> That same month, Carey released a duet with <a href="/wiki/John_Legend" title="John Legend">John Legend</a> titled "<a href="/wiki/When_Christmas_Comes" title="When Christmas Comes">When Christmas Comes</a>", originally part of <i>Merry Christmas II You</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-203"><a href="#cite_note-203"><span>[</span>203<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>On March 1, 2012, Carey performed at <a href="/wiki/New_York_City" title="New York City">New York City</a>'s Gotham Hall; her first time performing since pregnancy.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-204"><a href="#cite_note-204"><span>[</span>204<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-205"><a href="#cite_note-205"><span>[</span>205<span>]</span></a></sup> She also performed a three song set at a special fundraiser for US President <a href="/wiki/Barack_Obama" title="Barack Obama">Barack Obama</a> held in New York's Plaza Hotel. A new song titled "Bring It On Home", which Carey wrote specifically for the event to show her support behind Obama's re-election campaign, was also performed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-206"><a href="#cite_note-206"><span>[</span>206<span>]</span></a></sup> In August 2012, she released a stand alone single, "<a href="/wiki/Triumphant_(Get_%27Em)" title="Triumphant (Get 'Em)">Triumphant (Get 'Em)</a>", featuring American rappers <a href="/wiki/Rick_Ross" title="Rick Ross">Rick Ross</a> and <a href="/wiki/Meek_Mill" title="Meek Mill">Meek Mill</a> and co-written and co-produced by Carey, <a href="/wiki/Jermaine_Dupri" title="Jermaine Dupri">Jermaine Dupri</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Bryan-Michael_Cox" title="Bryan-Michael Cox">Bryan-Michael Cox</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-207"><a href="#cite_note-207"><span>[</span>207<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-208"><a href="#cite_note-208"><span>[</span>208<span>]</span></a></sup> Carey joined the judging panel of <i><a href="/wiki/American_Idol" title="American Idol">American Idol</a></i> season twelve as <a href="/wiki/Jennifer_Lopez" title="Jennifer Lopez">Jennifer Lopez</a>'s replacement, joining <a href="/wiki/Randy_Jackson" title="Randy Jackson">Randy Jackson</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nicki_Minaj" title="Nicki Minaj">Nicki Minaj</a> and <a href="/wiki/Keith_Urban" title="Keith Urban">Keith Urban</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-highestpaid_209-0"><a href="#cite_note-highestpaid-209"><span>[</span>209<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-210"><a href="#cite_note-210"><span>[</span>210<span>]</span></a></sup> In November 2013, she explained about hating to work at <i>American Idol</i> adding, "It was like going to work every day in hell with Satan", referring to her on-set squabbles with Minaj.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-211"><a href="#cite_note-211"><span>[</span>211<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-212"><a href="#cite_note-212"><span>[</span>212<span>]</span></a></sup> Carey appeared in <a href="/wiki/Lee_Daniels" title="Lee Daniels">Lee Daniels</a>' 2013 film <i><a href="/wiki/The_Butler" title="The Butler">The Butler</a></i>, about a <a href="/wiki/White_House" title="White House">White House</a> butler who served eight American Presidents over the course of three decades.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-213"><a href="#cite_note-213"><span>[</span>213<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-214"><a href="#cite_note-214"><span>[</span>214<span>]</span></a></sup> Carey made <a href="/wiki/Guest_appearance" title="Guest appearance">guest</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Voice_artist" title="Voice artist">voice</a>-star as a <a href="/wiki/Redneck" title="Redneck">redneck</a> character on the adult animated series <i><a href="/wiki/American_Dad!" title="American Dad!">American Dad!</a></i> on November 24, 2013.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-215"><a href="#cite_note-215"><span>[</span>215<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-216"><a href="#cite_note-216"><span>[</span>216<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>In February 2013 Carey recorded and released a song called "<a href="/wiki/Almost_Home_(Mariah_Carey_song)" title="Almost Home (Mariah Carey song)">Almost Home</a>", for the soundtrack of the <a href="/wiki/The_Walt_Disney_Studios_(division)" title="The Walt Disney Studios (division)">Walt Disney Studios</a> film <i><a href="/wiki/Oz_the_Great_and_Powerful" title="Oz the Great and Powerful">Oz the Great and Powerful</a></i>. The video was directed by photographer <a href="/wiki/David_LaChapelle" title="David LaChapelle">David LaChapelle</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-217"><a href="#cite_note-217"><span>[</span>217<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-218"><a href="#cite_note-218"><span>[</span>218<span>]</span></a></sup> News started coming around about the singer's fourteenth studio album.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-219"><a href="#cite_note-219"><span>[</span>219<span>]</span></a></sup> Some of the people that Carey worked with on the album included: <a href="/wiki/DJ_Clue%3F" title="DJ Clue?">DJ Clue?</a>, <a href="/wiki/Randy_Jackson" title="Randy Jackson">Randy Jackson</a>, <a href="/wiki/Q-Tip_(musician)" title="Q-Tip (musician)">Q-Tip</a>, <a href="/wiki/R._Kelly" title="R. Kelly">R. Kelly</a>, <a href="/wiki/David_Morales" title="David Morales">David Morales</a>, <a href="/wiki/Loris_Holland" title="Loris Holland">Loris Holland</a>, <a href="/wiki/Stevie_J" title="Stevie J">Stevie J</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/James_Fauntleroy_II" title="James Fauntleroy II">James Fauntleroy II</a>, Ray Angry, Afanasieff, Dupri, <a href="/wiki/Bryan-Michael_Cox" title="Bryan-Michael Cox">Bryan-Michael Cox</a>, James "Big Jim" Wright, <a href="/wiki/Hit-Boy" title="Hit-Boy">Hit-Boy</a>, <a href="/wiki/The-Dream" title="The-Dream">The-Dream</a>, <a href="/wiki/Da_Brat" title="Da Brat">Da Brat</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Rodney_Jerkins" title="Rodney Jerkins">Rodney Jerkins</a>. Carey told <i><a href="/wiki/Billboard_(magazine)" title="Billboard (magazine)">Billboard</a></i>: "It's about making sure I have tons of good music, because at the end of the day that's the most important thing... There are a lot more raw ballads than people might expect...there are also uptempo and signature-type songs that represent [my] different facets as an artist".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-220"><a href="#cite_note-220"><span>[</span>220<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>The lead single, "<a href="/wiki/Beautiful_(Mariah_Carey_song)" title="Beautiful (Mariah Carey song)">Beautiful</a>" featuring singer <a href="/wiki/Miguel_(singer)" title="Miguel (singer)">Miguel</a>, was released on May 6, 2013, and peaked at number 15 on the Hot 100.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-221"><a href="#cite_note-221"><span>[</span>221<span>]</span></a></sup> Carey taped a performance of "Beautiful" along with a medley of her greatest hits on May 15, 2013; the taping aired on the <i>American Idol</i> finale the following day.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-222"><a href="#cite_note-222"><span>[</span>222<span>]</span></a></sup> On October 14, 2013, Carey announced that the album's former <a href="/wiki/The_Art_of_Letting_Go" title="The Art of Letting Go">title track</a> has been chosen as the second single; it premiered via <a href="/wiki/Facebook" title="Facebook">Facebook</a> on November 11, 2013. During a Q&amp;A session following the song's release, Carey gave an update about the album, stating: "Now I've been inspired to add two more songs, so we're almost there. I can't even express this properly but I feel like this is gonna be my favorite album".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-223"><a href="#cite_note-223"><span>[</span>223<span>]</span></a></sup> Following another song release, "<a href="/wiki/You%27re_Mine_(Eternal)" title="You're Mine (Eternal)">You're Mine (Eternal)</a>",<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-224"><a href="#cite_note-224"><span>[</span>224<span>]</span></a></sup> it was announced that <i>The Art of Letting Go</i> would no longer be the title of the album.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-225"><a href="#cite_note-225"><span>[</span>225<span>]</span></a></sup> After the final name was announced, <i><a href="/wiki/Me._I_Am_Mariah..._The_Elusive_Chanteuse" title="Me. I Am Mariah... The Elusive Chanteuse">Me. I Am Mariah... The Elusive Chanteuse</a></i> was released on May 27, 2014.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-226"><a href="#cite_note-226"><span>[</span>226<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2015:_Residency_show_in_Las_Vegas_and_advancement_to_Epic_Records">2015: Residency show in Las Vegas and advancement to Epic Records</span></h3>
<p>On 15 January, Carey announced that she will be taking up <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Number_Ones_(Mariah_Carey_residency)" title="Number Ones (Mariah Carey residency)">residency</a> at <a href="/wiki/The_Colosseum_at_Caesars_Palace" title="The Colosseum at Caesars Palace">The Colosseum</a> at the <a href="/wiki/Caesars_Palace" title="Caesars Palace">Caesars Palace</a> hotel in <a href="/wiki/Las_Vegas" title="Las Vegas">Las Vegas</a>. She confirmed the residency deal in a pre-recorded interview on <i><a href="/wiki/The_Ellen_DeGeneres_Show" title="The Ellen DeGeneres Show">The Ellen DeGeneres Show</a></i>. Speaking of the residency, Carey said "I'm going to do my first ever residency in Vegas at Caesars. This is a special event for me. And again, I have to hope that the fans will enjoy this cause I'm gonna be performing, which was kind of inspired by my album <i><a href="/wiki/Number_1%27s_(Mariah_Carey_album)" title="Number 1's (Mariah Carey album)">#1's</a></i>, and this is now the updated version with eighteen of them. Hopefully other people will enjoy this. I've never done this before." She further commented "It's a new chapter for me and I'm just excited about it." To coincide with the residency, Carey is set to release <i>Mariah Carey's #1's</i>, a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Greatest_hits" title="Greatest hits">greatest hits</a> <a href="/wiki/Compilation_album" title="Compilation album">compilation</a> which will contain all of her eighteen <a href="/wiki/Billboard_Hot_100" title="Billboard Hot 100"><i>Billboard</i> Hot 100</a> number one singles. The confirmation comes after <a href="/wiki/Celine_Dion" title="Celine Dion">Celine Dion</a> announced that she has postponed dates of her residency at Caesars Palace to care for her husband, <a href="/wiki/Ren%C3%A9_Ang%C3%A9lil" title="René Angélil">René Angélil</a>, who is suffering from ill health.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-227"><a href="#cite_note-227"><span>[</span>227<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>On January 30, 2015, it was announced that Carey has left <a href="/wiki/Universal_Music_Group" title="Universal Music Group">Universal Music Group</a>'s Def Jam Recordings to re-unite with <a href="/wiki/L.A._Reid" title="L.A. Reid">L.A. Reid</a> and Sony Music via <a href="/wiki/Epic_Records" title="Epic Records">Epic Records</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-228"><a href="#cite_note-228"><span>[</span>228<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-229"><a href="#cite_note-229"><span>[</span>229<span>]</span></a></sup> Before even signing a recording contract with the label, Carey was said to have asked for a $3 million advance from Epic, which did not come to fruition.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Honesty_Hour_230-0"><a href="#cite_note-Honesty_Hour-230"><span>[</span>230<span>]</span></a></sup> Carey is also expected to re-release an updated edition of her <i>#1 '​s</i> compilation disc as her first release under Epic.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-231"><a href="#cite_note-231"><span>[</span>231<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Philanthropy_and_other_activities">Philanthropy and other activities</span></h2>
<p>Carey is a philanthropist who has been involved with several charitable organizations.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-fresh_232-0"><a href="#cite_note-fresh-232"><span>[</span>232<span>]</span></a></sup> She became associated with the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fresh_Air_Fund" title="Fresh Air Fund">Fresh Air Fund</a> in the early 1990s, and is the co-founder of a camp located in <a href="/wiki/Fishkill,_New_York" title="Fishkill, New York">Fishkill</a>, New York, that enables inner-city youth to embrace the arts and introduces them to career opportunities.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-fresh_232-1"><a href="#cite_note-fresh-232"><span>[</span>232<span>]</span></a></sup> The camp was called <a href="/wiki/The_Fresh_Air_Fund" title="The Fresh Air Fund">Camp Mariah</a> "for her generous support and dedication to Fresh Air children", and she received a Congressional Horizon Award for her youth-related charity work.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-233"><a href="#cite_note-233"><span>[</span>233<span>]</span></a></sup> Carey also donated royalties from her hits "<a href="/wiki/Hero_(Mariah_Carey_song)" title="Hero (Mariah Carey song)">Hero</a>" and "<a href="/wiki/One_Sweet_Day" title="One Sweet Day">One Sweet Day</a>" to charities.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-billboard2_234-0"><a href="#cite_note-billboard2-234"><span>[</span>234<span>]</span></a></sup> She is well-known nationally for her work with the <a href="/wiki/Make-A-Wish_Foundation" title="Make-A-Wish Foundation">Make-A-Wish Foundation</a> in granting the wishes of children with life-threatening illnesses, and in November 2006 she was awarded the Foundation's Wish Idol for her "extraordinary generosity and her many wish granting achievements".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-235"><a href="#cite_note-235"><span>[</span>235<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-236"><a href="#cite_note-236"><span>[</span>236<span>]</span></a></sup> Carey has volunteered for the <a href="/wiki/New_York_City_Police_Department" title="New York City Police Department">New York City Police</a> Athletic League and contributed to the <a href="/wiki/Obstetrics" title="Obstetrics">obstetrics</a> department of <a href="/wiki/NewYork%E2%80%93Presbyterian_Hospital" title="NewYork–Presbyterian Hospital">New York Presbyterian Hospital</a> Cornell Medical Center.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pre_237-0"><a href="#cite_note-pre-237"><span>[</span>237<span>]</span></a></sup> A percentage of the sales of <i>MTV Unplugged</i> was donated to various other charities.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pre_237-1"><a href="#cite_note-pre-237"><span>[</span>237<span>]</span></a></sup> In 2008, Carey was named Hunger Ambassador of the <a href="/wiki/World_Food_Programme" title="World Food Programme">World Hunger Relief Movement</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-238"><a href="#cite_note-238"><span>[</span>238<span>]</span></a></sup> In February 2010, the song, "<a href="/wiki/100%25_(Mariah_Carey_song)" title="100% (Mariah Carey song)">100%</a>", which was originally written and recorded for the film, <i>Precious</i>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-239"><a href="#cite_note-239"><span>[</span>239<span>]</span></a></sup> was used as one of the theme songs for the <a href="/wiki/2010_Winter_Olympics" title="2010 Winter Olympics">2010 Winter Olympics</a>, with all money proceeds going to <a href="/wiki/United_States_Olympic_Committee" title="United States Olympic Committee">Team USA</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-240"><a href="#cite_note-240"><span>[</span>240<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>One of Carey's most high-profile benefit concert appearances was on VH1's 1998 <i><a href="/wiki/VH1_Divas" title="VH1 Divas">Divas Live</a></i> special, during which she performed alongside other female singers in support of the Save the Music Foundation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-divas_95-1"><a href="#cite_note-divas-95"><span>[</span>95<span>]</span></a></sup> The concert was a ratings success, and Carey participated in the <a href="/wiki/VH1_Divas#Divas_2000" title="VH1 Divas">Divas 2000</a> special.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-divas_95-2"><a href="#cite_note-divas-95"><span>[</span>95<span>]</span></a></sup> In 2007, the Save the Music Foundation honored Carey at their tenth gala event for her support towards the foundation since its inception.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated4_241-0"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated4-241"><span>[</span>241<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-242"><a href="#cite_note-242"><span>[</span>242<span>]</span></a></sup> She appeared at the <i><a href="/wiki/America:_A_Tribute_to_Heroes" title="America: A Tribute to Heroes">America: A Tribute to Heroes</a></i> nationally televised fundraiser in the aftermath of the <a href="/wiki/September_11_attacks" title="September 11 attacks">September 11 attacks</a>, and in December 2001, she performed before peacekeeping troops in <a href="/wiki/Kosovo" title="Kosovo">Kosovo</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-243"><a href="#cite_note-243"><span>[</span>243<span>]</span></a></sup> Carey hosted the <a href="/wiki/CBS" title="CBS">CBS</a> television special <i>At Home for the Holidays</i>, which documented real-life stories of adopted children and foster families.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-244"><a href="#cite_note-244"><span>[</span>244<span>]</span></a></sup> In 2005, Carey performed for <a href="/wiki/Live_8_concert,_London" title="Live 8 concert, London">Live 8 in London</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bbcnews_245-0"><a href="#cite_note-bbcnews-245"><span>[</span>245<span>]</span></a></sup> and at the <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Katrina" title="Hurricane Katrina">Hurricane Katrina</a> relief telethon "Shelter from the Storm".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-246"><a href="#cite_note-246"><span>[</span>246<span>]</span></a></sup> In August 2008, Carey and other singers recorded the charity single, "<a href="/wiki/Just_Stand_Up!" title="Just Stand Up!">Just Stand Up</a>" produced by <a href="/wiki/Babyface_(musician)" title="Babyface (musician)">Babyface</a> and <a href="/wiki/L.A._Reid" title="L.A. Reid">L. A. Reid</a>, to support "<a href="/wiki/Stand_Up_to_Cancer" title="Stand Up to Cancer">Stand Up to Cancer</a>".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-247"><a href="#cite_note-247"><span>[</span>247<span>]</span></a></sup> In 2008, Carey performed in a New Year's Eve concert for the family of Libyan dictator <a href="/wiki/Muammar_Gaddafi" title="Muammar Gaddafi">Muammar Gaddafi</a>, something she later claimed to "feel horrible and embarrassed to have participated in".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-248"><a href="#cite_note-248"><span>[</span>248<span>]</span></a></sup> In March 2011, Carey's representative Cindi Berger stated that royalties for the song "Save The Day", which was written for her fourteenth studio album, will be donated to charities that create awareness to human rights issues to make amends for the Gadaffi error. Berger also said that "Mariah has and continues to donate her time, money and countless hours of personal service to many organizations both here and abroad".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-billboard2_234-1"><a href="#cite_note-billboard2-234"><span>[</span>234<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Declining offers to appear in commercials in the United States during her early career, Carey was not involved in brand marketing initiatives until 2006, when she participated in endorsements for <a href="/wiki/Intel" title="Intel">Intel</a> <a href="/wiki/Centrino" title="Centrino">Centrino</a> personal computers and launched a jewelry and accessories line for teenagers, Glamorized, in American <a href="/wiki/Claire%27s" title="Claire's">Claire's</a> and Icing stores.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-249"><a href="#cite_note-249"><span>[</span>249<span>]</span></a></sup> During this period, as part of a partnership with <a href="/wiki/Pepsi" title="Pepsi">Pepsi</a> and <a href="/wiki/Motorola" title="Motorola">Motorola</a>, Carey recorded and promoted a series of exclusive <a href="/wiki/Ringtone" title="Ringtone">ringtones</a>, including "<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Time_of_Your_Life_(ring_tone)" title="Time of Your Life (ring tone)">Time of Your Life</a>".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-250"><a href="#cite_note-250"><span>[</span>250<span>]</span></a></sup> She signed a licensing deal with the cosmetics company <a href="/wiki/Elizabeth_Arden" title="Elizabeth Arden">Elizabeth Arden</a>, and in 2007, she released her own fragrance, "<a href="/wiki/M_(fragrance)" title="M (fragrance)">M</a>".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mtv1_251-0"><a href="#cite_note-mtv1-251"><span>[</span>251<span>]</span></a></sup> In 2007, <i><a href="/wiki/Forbes" title="Forbes">Forbes</a></i> named her as the fifth richest woman in entertainment, with an estimated net worth of US$270 million.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-namerer_252-0"><a href="#cite_note-namerer-252"><span>[</span>252<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-253"><a href="#cite_note-253"><span>[</span>253<span>]</span></a></sup> In November 2011, it was reported that Carey's net worth was valued at more than $500 million.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-enter_2-1"><a href="#cite_note-enter-2"><span>[</span>2<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-highestpaid_209-1"><a href="#cite_note-highestpaid-209"><span>[</span>209<span>]</span></a></sup> On November 29, 2010, she debuted a collection on <a href="/wiki/Home_Shopping_Network" title="Home Shopping Network">HSN</a>, which included jewelry, shoes and fragrances.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-254"><a href="#cite_note-254"><span>[</span>254<span>]</span></a></sup> In November 2011, Carey was announced as the new global ambassador for <a href="/wiki/Jenny_Craig,_Inc." title="Jenny Craig, Inc.">Jenny Craig</a>, following her weight loss with the program after giving birth to fraternal twins in April. Carey claims she lost 70 pounds (32 kg) on the program.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-dailymail-2059911_255-0"><a href="#cite_note-dailymail-2059911-255"><span>[</span>255<span>]</span></a></sup> In 2013, human rights activists criticized Carey for performing in a concert for <a href="/wiki/Angola" title="Angola">Angola</a>'s "father-daughter kleptocracy" and accused her of accepting "dictator cash".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-256"><a href="#cite_note-256"><span>[</span>256<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Artistry">Artistry</span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Musical_style">Musical style</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Mariah_Carey13_Edwards_Dec_1998.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1174" data-file-width="1186" height="218" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/Mariah_Carey13_Edwards_Dec_1998.jpg/220px-Mariah_Carey13_Edwards_Dec_1998.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/Mariah_Carey13_Edwards_Dec_1998.jpg/330px-Mariah_Carey13_Edwards_Dec_1998.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/Mariah_Carey13_Edwards_Dec_1998.jpg/440px-Mariah_Carey13_Edwards_Dec_1998.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Mariah_Carey13_Edwards_Dec_1998.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Carey at Edwards Air Force Base during the making of "I Still Believe" video in 1998</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Love is the subject of the majority of Carey's lyrics, although she has written about themes such as racism, <a href="/wiki/Social_alienation" title="Social alienation">social alienation</a>, death, <a href="/wiki/Malnutrition" title="Malnutrition">world hunger</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Spirituality" title="Spirituality">spirituality</a>. She has said that much of her work is partly autobiographical, but <i><a href="/wiki/Time_(magazine)" title="Time (magazine)">Time</a></i> magazine wrote: "If only Mariah Carey's music had the drama of her life. Her songs are often sugary and artificial—<a href="/wiki/NutraSweet" title="NutraSweet">NutraSweet</a> soul. But her life has passion and conflict," applying it to the first stages of her career. He commented that as her albums progressed, so too her songwriting and music blossomed into more mature and meaningful material.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-time_257-0"><a href="#cite_note-time-257"><span>[</span>257<span>]</span></a></sup> Jim Faber of the <i><a href="/wiki/Daily_News_(New_York)" title="Daily News (New York)">New York Daily News</a></i>, made similar comments, "For Carey, vocalizing is all about the performance, not the emotions that inspired it. Singing, to her, represents a physical challenge, not an emotional unburdening."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-258"><a href="#cite_note-258"><span>[</span>258<span>]</span></a></sup> While reviewing <i>Music Box</i>, Stephen Holden from <i><a href="/wiki/Rolling_Stone" title="Rolling Stone">Rolling Stone</a></i> commented that Carey sang with "sustained passion", while Arion Berger of <i><a href="/wiki/Entertainment_Weekly" title="Entertainment Weekly">Entertainment Weekly</a></i> wrote that during some vocal moments, Carey becomes "too overwhelmed to put her passion into words."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-259"><a href="#cite_note-259"><span>[</span>259<span>]</span></a></sup> In 2001, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Village_Voice" title="The Village Voice">The Village Voice</a></i> wrote in regards to what they considered Carey's "centerless ballads", writing, "Carey's <a href="/wiki/Strawberry_Shortcake" title="Strawberry Shortcake">Strawberry Shortcake</a> soul still provides the template with which <a href="/wiki/Teen_pop" title="Teen pop">teen-pop</a> cuties draw curlicues around those centerless <a href="/wiki/Diane_Warren" title="Diane Warren">[Diane] Warren</a> ballads [.....] it's largely because of [Blige] that the new R&amp;B demands a greater range of emotional expression, smarter poetry, more from-the-gut testifying, and less [sic] unnecessary notes than the squeaky-clean and just plain squeaky Mariah era. Nowadays it's the <a href="/wiki/Christina_Aguilera" title="Christina Aguilera">Christina Aguileras</a> and <a href="/wiki/Jessica_Simpson" title="Jessica Simpson">Jessica Simpsons</a> who awkwardly oversing, while the women with roof-raising lung power keep it in check when tune or lyric demands."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-260"><a href="#cite_note-260"><span>[</span>260<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Carey's output makes use of <a href="/wiki/Electronic_musical_instrument" title="Electronic musical instrument">electronic instruments</a> such as <a href="/wiki/Drum_machine" title="Drum machine">drum machines</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-viber_140-2"><a href="#cite_note-viber-140"><span>[</span>140<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Electronic_keyboard" title="Electronic keyboard">keyboards</a> and synthesizers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pop_261-0"><a href="#cite_note-pop-261"><span>[</span>261<span>]</span></a></sup> Many of her songs contain piano-driven melodies,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rs_262-0"><a href="#cite_note-rs-262"><span>[</span>262<span>]</span></a></sup> as she was given piano lessons when she was six years old.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nick3_9-2"><a href="#cite_note-nick3-9"><span>[</span>9<span>]</span></a></sup> Carey said that she cannot read <a href="/wiki/Sheet_music" title="Sheet music">sheet music</a> and prefers to collaborate with a pianist when composing her material, but feels that it is easier to experiment with faster and less conventional <a href="/wiki/Melody" title="Melody">melodies</a> and <a href="/wiki/Chord_progression" title="Chord progression">chord progressions</a> using this technique.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nick3_9-3"><a href="#cite_note-nick3-9"><span>[</span>9<span>]</span></a></sup> While Carey learned to play the piano at a young age, and incorporates several ranges of production and instrumentation into her music, she has maintained that her voice has always been her most important asset: "My voice is my instrument; it always has been."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-shapiro20_91-2"><a href="#cite_note-shapiro20-91"><span>[</span>91<span>]</span></a></sup> Carey began commissioning <a href="/wiki/Remix" title="Remix">remixes</a> of her material early in her career and helped to spearhead the practice of recording entirely new vocals for remixes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MTV-Oct2003_263-0"><a href="#cite_note-MTV-Oct2003-263"><span>[</span>263<span>]</span></a></sup> Disc jockey <a href="/wiki/David_Morales" title="David Morales">David Morales</a> has collaborated with Carey on several occasions, starting with "<a href="/wiki/Dreamlover_(song)" title="Dreamlover (song)">Dreamlover</a>" (1993), which popularized the tradition of remixing R&amp;B songs into <a href="/wiki/House_music" title="House music">house</a> records, and which <i><a href="/wiki/Slant_Magazine" title="Slant Magazine">Slant</a></i> magazine named one of the greatest dance songs of all time.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-264"><a href="#cite_note-264"><span>[</span>264<span>]</span></a></sup> From "<a href="/wiki/Fantasy_(Mariah_Carey_song)" title="Fantasy (Mariah Carey song)">Fantasy</a>" (1995) onward, Carey enlisted both hip-hop and house producers to re-structure her album compositions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-shapiro17_80-2"><a href="#cite_note-shapiro17-80"><span>[</span>80<span>]</span></a></sup> <i>Entertainment Weekly</i> included two remixes of "Fantasy" on a list of Carey's greatest recordings compiled in 2005: a National Dance Music Award-winning remix produced by Morales, and a <a href="/wiki/Sean_Combs" title="Sean Combs">Sean Combs</a> production featuring rapper <a href="/wiki/Ol%27_Dirty_Bastard" title="Ol' Dirty Bastard">Ol' Dirty Bastard</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-265"><a href="#cite_note-265"><span>[</span>265<span>]</span></a></sup> The latter has been credited with popularizing the R&amp;B/hip-hop collaboration trend that has continued into the 2000s, through artists such as <a href="/wiki/Ashanti_(singer)" title="Ashanti (singer)">Ashanti</a> and <a href="/wiki/Beyonc%C3%A9" title="Beyoncé">Beyoncé</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MTV-Oct2003_263-1"><a href="#cite_note-MTV-Oct2003-263"><span>[</span>263<span>]</span></a></sup> Combs said that Carey "knows the importance of mixes, so you feel like you're with an artist who appreciates your work—an artist who wants to come up with something with you".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-viberness_266-0"><a href="#cite_note-viberness-266"><span>[</span>266<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Voice_and_timbre">Voice and timbre</span></h3>
<div class="quotebox" style="float: right; clear: right; margin: 0.5em 0 0.8em 1.4em; width:350px; padding: 6px; border: 1px solid #aaa; font-size: 88%; background-color: #F9F9F9;">
<div class="" style="position: relative; text-align: left;">
<div>
<p>"I have <a href="/wiki/Vocal_fold_nodule" title="Vocal fold nodule">nodules</a> on my vocal cords. My mother says I've had them since I was a kid. That's why I have the high register and the belting register and I can still be husky. A lot of people couldn't sing through the nodules the way I do; I've learned to sing <i>through</i> my vocal cords. The only thing that really affects my voice is sleep. Sometimes if I'm exhausted, I can't hit the really high notes. My doctors showed me my vocal cords and why I can hit those high notes. It's a certain part of the cord that not many people use—the very top. My natural voice is low. I have a raspy voice. I'm really more of an <a href="/wiki/Alto" title="Alto">alto</a>. But my airy voice can be high if I'm rested. [...] When I was little, I'd talk in this really high whisper, and my mom would be like, 'You're being ridiculous'. I thought if I can talk like that I can sing like that. So I started just messing around with it. I'd practice and practice, and she'd be like, 'You're gonna hurt yourself'. I'd tell her, it doesn't hurt. If I were to try and belt two octaves lower than that, that would be a strain."</p>
</div>
</div>
<div style="text-align: left;">—Carey on her usage of the <a href="/wiki/Whistle_register" title="Whistle register">whistle register</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-vinsky_99-1"><a href="#cite_note-vinsky-99"><span>[</span>99<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-267"><a href="#cite_note-267"><span>[</span>267<span>]</span></a></sup></div>
</div>
<p>Carey possesses a <a href="/wiki/Vocal_range" title="Vocal range">five-octave vocal range</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated6_268-0"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated6-268"><span>[</span>268<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-269"><a href="#cite_note-269"><span>[</span>269<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-270"><a href="#cite_note-270"><span>[</span>270<span>]</span></a></sup> and has the ability to reach notes beyond the 7th octave.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-271"><a href="#cite_note-271"><span>[</span>271<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-272"><a href="#cite_note-272"><span>[</span>272<span>]</span></a></sup> Referred to as the "songbird supreme" by the <i><a href="/wiki/Guinness_World_Records" title="Guinness World Records">Guinness World Records</a></i>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-James_273-0"><a href="#cite_note-James-273"><span>[</span>273<span>]</span></a></sup> she was ranked first in a 2003 MTV and <i><a href="/wiki/Blender_(magazine)" title="Blender (magazine)">Blender</a></i> magazine countdown of the 22 Greatest Voices in Music, as voted by fans and readers in an online poll. Carey said of the poll, "What it really means is voice of the MTV generation. Of course, it's an enormous compliment, but I don't feel that way about myself."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-274"><a href="#cite_note-274"><span>[</span>274<span>]</span></a></sup> She also placed second in <i>Cove</i> magazine's list of "The 100 Outstanding Pop Vocalists".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-100_Outstanding_Pop_Vocalists_275-0"><a href="#cite_note-100_Outstanding_Pop_Vocalists-275"><span>[</span>275<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Regarding her <a href="/wiki/Voice_type" title="Voice type">voice type</a>, Carey said that she is an <a href="/wiki/Alto" title="Alto">alto</a>, though several critics have described her as a <a href="/wiki/Soprano" title="Soprano">soprano</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-276"><a href="#cite_note-276"><span>[</span>276<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-277"><a href="#cite_note-277"><span>[</span>277<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-books.google.ca_278-0"><a href="#cite_note-books.google.ca-278"><span>[</span>278<span>]</span></a></sup> However, within contemporary forms of music, singers are classified by the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Music_style" title="Music style">style of music</a> they sing. There is currently no authoritative voice classification system within non-classical music.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Peckham_279-0"><a href="#cite_note-Peckham-279"><span>[</span>279<span>]</span></a></sup> Attempts have been made to adopt classical voice type terms to other forms of singing, but they are controversial,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Peckham_279-1"><a href="#cite_note-Peckham-279"><span>[</span>279<span>]</span></a></sup> because the development of classical voice categorizations were made with the understanding that the singer would amplify his or her voice with their natural resonators, without a <a href="/wiki/Microphone" title="Microphone">microphone</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Appleman_280-0"><a href="#cite_note-Appleman-280"><span>[</span>280<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Jon_Pareles" title="Jon Pareles">Jon Pareles</a> of <i>The New York Times</i> described Carey's lower register as a "rich, husky alto" that extends to "dog-whistle high notes".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nytreview_281-0"><a href="#cite_note-nytreview-281"><span>[</span>281<span>]</span></a></sup> Additionally, towards the late 1990s, Carey began incorporating <a href="/wiki/Breathy_voice" title="Breathy voice">breathy vocals</a> into her material.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-charm_282-0"><a href="#cite_note-charm-282"><span>[</span>282<span>]</span></a></sup> Tim Levell from the BBC News described her vocals as "sultry close-to-the-mic breathiness",<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-charm_282-1"><a href="#cite_note-charm-282"><span>[</span>282<span>]</span></a></sup> while <i>USA Today</i> '​s Elysa Gardner wrote "it's impossible to deny the impact her vocal style, a florid blend of breathy riffing and resonant belting, has had on today's young pop and R&amp;B stars."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-gold_283-0"><a href="#cite_note-gold-283"><span>[</span>283<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Sasha Frere-Jones of <i><a href="/wiki/The_New_Yorker" title="The New Yorker">The New Yorker</a></i> adds her <a href="/wiki/Timbre" title="Timbre">timbre</a> possesses various colors, saying, "Carey's sound changes with nearly every line, mutating from a steely tone to a vibrating growl and then to a humid, breathy coo. Her wide vocal range allows Carey to take melodies from alto bottom notes to coloratura soprano upper register."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-newyorker_62-2"><a href="#cite_note-newyorker-62"><span>[</span>62<span>]</span></a></sup> Carey also possesses a "whisper register". In an interview with the singer, Ron Givens of <i>Entertainment Weekly</i> described it this way, "first, a rippling, soulful ooh comes rolling effortlessly from her throat: alto. Then, after a quick breath, she goes for the stratosphere, with a sound that nearly changes the barometric pressure in the room. In one brief swoop, she seems to squeal and roar at the same time."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-284"><a href="#cite_note-284"><span>[</span>284<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Her sense of pitch is admired<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nytreview_281-1"><a href="#cite_note-nytreview-281"><span>[</span>281<span>]</span></a></sup> and Jon Pareles adds "she can linger over sensual turns, growl with playful confidence, syncopate like a <a href="/wiki/Scat_singing" title="Scat singing">scat singer</a>... with startlingly exact pitch."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nytreview_281-2"><a href="#cite_note-nytreview-281"><span>[</span>281<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Influences">Influences</span></h3>
<p>Carey has said that from childhood she has been influenced by <a href="/wiki/Billie_Holiday" title="Billie Holiday">Billie Holiday</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sarah_Vaughan" title="Sarah Vaughan">Sarah Vaughan</a>, and R&amp;B and soul musicians such as <a href="/wiki/Gladys_Knight" title="Gladys Knight">Gladys Knight</a> and <a href="/wiki/Aretha_Franklin" title="Aretha Franklin">Aretha Franklin</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-black_285-0"><a href="#cite_note-black-285"><span>[</span>285<span>]</span></a></sup> Her music contains strong influences of <a href="/wiki/Gospel_music" title="Gospel music">gospel music</a>, and she credits <a href="/wiki/The_Clark_Sisters" title="The Clark Sisters">The Clark Sisters</a>, <a href="/wiki/Shirley_Caesar" title="Shirley Caesar">Shirley Caesar</a> and <a href="/wiki/Edwin_Hawkins" title="Edwin Hawkins">Edwin Hawkins</a> as the most influential in her early years.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-black_285-1"><a href="#cite_note-black-285"><span>[</span>285<span>]</span></a></sup> When Carey incorporated hip-hop into her sound, speculation arose that she was making an attempt to take advantage of the genre's popularity, but she told <i><a href="/wiki/Newsweek" title="Newsweek">Newsweek</a></i>, "People just don't understand. I grew up with this music".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEShapiro2001124_286-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEShapiro2001124-286"><span>[</span>286<span>]</span></a></sup> She has expressed appreciation for rappers such as <a href="/wiki/The_Sugarhill_Gang" title="The Sugarhill Gang">The Sugarhill Gang</a>, <a href="/wiki/Eric_B._%26_Rakim" title="Eric B. &amp; Rakim">Eric B. &amp; Rakim</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Wu-Tang_Clan" title="Wu-Tang Clan">Wu-Tang Clan</a>, <a href="/wiki/The_Notorious_B.I.G." title="The Notorious B.I.G.">The Notorious B.I.G.</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mobb_Deep" title="Mobb Deep">Mobb Deep</a>, with whom she collaborated on the single "<a href="/wiki/The_Roof_(Back_in_Time)" title="The Roof (Back in Time)">The Roof (Back in Time)</a>" (1998).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-vinsky_99-2"><a href="#cite_note-vinsky-99"><span>[</span>99<span>]</span></a></sup> Carey was heavily influenced by <a href="/wiki/Minnie_Riperton" title="Minnie Riperton">Minnie Riperton</a>, and began experimenting with the whistle register due to her original practice of the range.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-vinsky_99-3"><a href="#cite_note-vinsky-99"><span>[</span>99<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>During Carey's career, her vocal and musical style, along with her level of success, has been compared to <a href="/wiki/Whitney_Houston" title="Whitney Houston">Whitney Houston</a>, who she has also cited as an influence,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOX_287-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOX-287"><span>[</span>287<span>]</span></a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Celine_Dion" title="Celine Dion">Celine Dion</a>. Carey and her peers, according to Garry Mulholland, are "the princesses of wails [...] virtuoso vocalists who blend chart-oriented pop with mature <a href="/wiki/Middle_of_the_road_(music)" title="Middle of the road (music)">MOR</a> <a href="/wiki/Torch_song" title="Torch song">torch song</a>".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Mul_288-0"><a href="#cite_note-Mul-288"><span>[</span>288<span>]</span></a></sup> Author and writer Lucy O'Brien attributed the comeback of <a href="/wiki/Barbra_Streisand" title="Barbra Streisand">Barbra Streisand</a>'s "old-fashioned showgirl" to Carey and Dion, and described them and Houston as "groomed, airbrushed and overblown to perfection".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Mul_288-1"><a href="#cite_note-Mul-288"><span>[</span>288<span>]</span></a></sup> Carey's musical transition and use of more revealing clothing during the late 1990s were, in part, initiated to distance herself from this image, and she subsequently said that most of her early work was "schmaltzy MOR".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Mul_288-2"><a href="#cite_note-Mul-288"><span>[</span>288<span>]</span></a></sup> Some have noted that unlike Houston and Dion, Carey co-writes and produces her own songs.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-James_273-1"><a href="#cite_note-James-273"><span>[</span>273<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Legacy">Legacy</span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Mariah_Carey_Neighborhood_Ball_in_downtown_Washington_2009_cropped.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2004" data-file-width="2688" height="164" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/da/Mariah_Carey_Neighborhood_Ball_in_downtown_Washington_2009_cropped.JPG/220px-Mariah_Carey_Neighborhood_Ball_in_downtown_Washington_2009_cropped.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/da/Mariah_Carey_Neighborhood_Ball_in_downtown_Washington_2009_cropped.JPG/330px-Mariah_Carey_Neighborhood_Ball_in_downtown_Washington_2009_cropped.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/da/Mariah_Carey_Neighborhood_Ball_in_downtown_Washington_2009_cropped.JPG/440px-Mariah_Carey_Neighborhood_Ball_in_downtown_Washington_2009_cropped.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Mariah_Carey_Neighborhood_Ball_in_downtown_Washington_2009_cropped.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Carey performing "<a href="/wiki/Hero_(Mariah_Carey_song)" title="Hero (Mariah Carey song)">Hero</a>" live during The Neighborhood Inaugural Ball for President Obama</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Carey's vocal style and singing ability have significantly impacted popular and contemporary music. As music critic G. Brown from <i><a href="/wiki/The_Denver_Post" title="The Denver Post">The Denver Post</a></i> wrote, "For better or worse, Mariah Carey's five-octave range and melismatic style have influenced a generation of pop singers."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-289"><a href="#cite_note-289"><span>[</span>289<span>]</span></a></sup> According to <i>Rolling Stone</i>, "Her mastery of melisma, the fluttering strings of notes that decorate songs like "<a href="/wiki/Vision_of_Love" title="Vision of Love">Vision of Love</a>", inspired the entire <i><a href="/wiki/American_Idol" title="American Idol">American Idol</a></i> vocal school, for better or worse, and virtually every other female R&amp;B singer since the Nineties."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-great_290-0"><a href="#cite_note-great-290"><span>[</span>290<span>]</span></a></sup> Jody Rosen of <i><a href="/wiki/Slate_(magazine)" title="Slate (magazine)">Slate</a></i> wrote of Carey's influence in modern music, calling her the most influential vocal stylist of the last two decades, the person who made rococo melismatic singing.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-slate.com_291-0"><a href="#cite_note-slate.com-291"><span>[</span>291<span>]</span></a></sup> Rosen further exemplified Carey's influence by drawing parallel with American Idol, which to her, "often played out as a clash of melisma-mad Mariah wannabes. And, today, nearly 20 years after Carey's debut, major labels continue to bet the farm on young stars such as the winner of Britain's X Factor show, <a href="/wiki/Leona_Lewis" title="Leona Lewis">Leona Lewis</a>, with her Generation Next gloss on Mariah's big voice and big hair."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-slate.com_291-1"><a href="#cite_note-slate.com-291"><span>[</span>291<span>]</span></a></sup> Sean Daly of <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/St._Petersburg_Times" title="St. Petersburg Times">St. Petersburg Times</a></i> wrote, "Depending on how you feel about public humiliation, the best/worst parts of American Idol are the audition shows, which normally break down into three distinct parts:(1) The Talented Kids.(2) The Weird Kids.(3) The Mariahs." Daly further commented, "The Mariahs are the hardest ones to watch, mainly because most of them think they're reeeaaally good. The poor, disillusioned hopefuls plant themselves in front of judges <a href="/wiki/Simon_Cowell" title="Simon Cowell">Simon Cowell</a>, <a href="/wiki/Paula_Abdul" title="Paula Abdul">Paula Abdul</a> and <a href="/wiki/Randy_Jackson" title="Randy Jackson">Randy Jackson</a> – then proceed to stretch, break and mutilate every note of a song, often Mariah's Hero, a tune that has ruined more throats than smoker's cough."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-npr.org_292-0"><a href="#cite_note-npr.org-292"><span>[</span>292<span>]</span></a></sup> <i>New York Magazine's</i> editor Roger Deckker said that in regarding Carey as an influential artist in music, he commented that "Whitney Houston may have introduced melisma (the vocally acrobatic style of lending a word an extra syllable or twenty) to the charts, but it was Mariah—with her jaw-dropping range—who made it into America's default sound." Deckker also added that "Every time you turn on American Idol, you are watching her children".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nymag1_293-0"><a href="#cite_note-nymag1-293"><span>[</span>293<span>]</span></a></sup> Despite her vocal prowess, Carey's vocal technique particularly with the use of <a href="/wiki/Melisma" title="Melisma">melisma</a> and <a href="/wiki/Belting_(music)" title="Belting (music)">belting</a>, has been subject to public scrutiny mainly because of young singers such as from talent shows have been overly imitating her singing technique in which critics commented "Mariah Carey is, without a doubt, the worst thing to happen to amateur singing since the karaoke machine".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-npr.org_292-1"><a href="#cite_note-npr.org-292"><span>[</span>292<span>]</span></a></sup> As Professor Katherine L. Meizel noted in her book, <i>The Mediation of Identity Politics in American Idol</i>, "Carey's influence not just stops in the emulation of melisma or her singing amongst the wannabe's, it's also her persona, her diva, her stardom which inspires them.... a pre-fame conic look."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-294"><a href="#cite_note-294"><span>[</span>294<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Among the hip hop, pop, and R&amp;B artists who have cited Carey as an influence are; <a href="/wiki/Aneeka" title="Aneeka">Aneeka</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-aneeka-recording_295-0"><a href="#cite_note-aneeka-recording-295"><span>[</span>295<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Ariana_Grande" title="Ariana Grande">Ariana Grande</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Influences1_296-0"><a href="#cite_note-Influences1-296"><span>[</span>296<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Britney_Spears" title="Britney Spears">Britney Spears</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-297"><a href="#cite_note-297"><span>[</span>297<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Beyonc%C3%A9" title="Beyoncé">Beyoncé</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-newyorker_62-3"><a href="#cite_note-newyorker-62"><span>[</span>62<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Christina_Aguilera" title="Christina Aguilera">Christina Aguilera</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-vol_298-0"><a href="#cite_note-vol-298"><span>[</span>298<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Jessica_Simpson" title="Jessica Simpson">Jessica Simpson</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-gold_283-1"><a href="#cite_note-gold-283"><span>[</span>283<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Rihanna" title="Rihanna">Rihanna</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mtv.com_299-0"><a href="#cite_note-mtv.com-299"><span>[</span>299<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Grimes_(musician)" title="Grimes (musician)">Grimes</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-300"><a href="#cite_note-300"><span>[</span>300<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Kelly_Clarkson" title="Kelly Clarkson">Kelly Clarkson</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-301"><a href="#cite_note-301"><span>[</span>301<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Nelly_Furtado" title="Nelly Furtado">Nelly Furtado</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-302"><a href="#cite_note-302"><span>[</span>302<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Leona_Lewis" title="Leona Lewis">Leona Lewis</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-303"><a href="#cite_note-303"><span>[</span>303<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Brandy_Norwood" title="Brandy Norwood">Brandy Norwood</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-great_290-1"><a href="#cite_note-great-290"><span>[</span>290<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Pink_(singer)" title="Pink (singer)">Pink</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-304"><a href="#cite_note-304"><span>[</span>304<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Mary_J._Blige" title="Mary J. Blige">Mary J. Blige</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-305"><a href="#cite_note-305"><span>[</span>305<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Melanie_Fiona" title="Melanie Fiona">Melanie Fiona</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated10_306-0"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated10-306"><span>[</span>306<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Missy_Elliott" title="Missy Elliott">Missy Elliott</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-newyorker_62-4"><a href="#cite_note-newyorker-62"><span>[</span>62<span>]</span></a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Jessica_Sanchez" title="Jessica Sanchez">Jessica Sanchez</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-307"><a href="#cite_note-307"><span>[</span>307<span>]</span></a></sup> According to <a href="/wiki/Stevie_Wonder" title="Stevie Wonder">Stevie Wonder</a>, "When people talk about the great influential singers, they talk about <a href="/wiki/Aretha_Franklin" title="Aretha Franklin">Aretha</a>, <a href="/wiki/Whitney_Houston" title="Whitney Houston">Whitney</a> and Mariah. That's a testament to her talent. Her range is that amazing."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-vibe_112-1"><a href="#cite_note-vibe-112"><span>[</span>112<span>]</span></a></sup> Beyoncé credits Carey's singing and her song "Vision of Love" as influencing her to begin practicing vocal "runs" as a child, as well as helping her pursue a career as a musician.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-newyorker_62-5"><a href="#cite_note-newyorker-62"><span>[</span>62<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Rihanna" title="Rihanna">Rihanna</a> has stated that Carey is one of her major influences and idol.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mtv.com_299-1"><a href="#cite_note-mtv.com-299"><span>[</span>299<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Christina_Aguilera" title="Christina Aguilera">Christina Aguilera</a> said in the early stages of her career that Carey was a big influence in her singing career and one of her idols.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-vol_298-1"><a href="#cite_note-vol-298"><span>[</span>298<span>]</span></a></sup> According to Pier Dominguez, author of <i>Christina Aguilera: A star is made</i>, Aguilera has stated how she loved listening to <a href="/wiki/Whitney_Houston" title="Whitney Houston">Whitney Houston</a>, but it was Carey who had the biggest influence on her vocal styling. Carey's carefully choreographed image of a grown woman struck a chord with Aguilera. Her influence on Aguilera also grew from the fact that both are of mixed heritage.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-308"><a href="#cite_note-308"><span>[</span>308<span>]</span></a></sup> Philip Brasor, editor of <i><a href="/wiki/The_Japan_Times" title="The Japan Times">The Japan Times</a></i>, expressed how Carey's vocal and melismatic style even influenced Asian singers. He wrote that Japanese singer <a href="/wiki/Hikaru_Utada" title="Hikaru Utada">Utada Hikaru</a> "sang what she heard, from the diaphragm and with her own take on the kind of melisma that became de rigueur in American pop after the ascendance of Mariah Carey."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-309"><a href="#cite_note-309"><span>[</span>309<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>In an article titled "Out With Mariah's Melisma, In With Kesha's Kick", writer <a href="/wiki/David_Browne" title="David Browne">David Browne</a> of <i><a href="/wiki/The_New_York_Times" title="The New York Times">The New York Times</a></i> discusses how the once ubiquitous <a href="/wiki/Melisma" title="Melisma">melisma</a> pop style suddenly lost in favor of the now ubiquitous <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Autotune" title="Autotune">autotune</a> in which the former was heavily popularized by the likes of Mariah Carey and Whitney Houston. Browne had commented "But beginning two decades ago, melisma overtook pop in a way it hadn't before. Mariah Carey's debut hit from 1990, "Vision of Love," followed two years later by Whitney Houston's version of "I Will Always Love You," set the bar insanely high for notes stretched louder, longer and knottier than most pop fans had ever heard." Browne further added "A subsequent generation of singers, including Ms. Aguilera, Jennifer Hudson and Beyoncé, built their careers around melisma. (Men like Brian McKnight and Tyrese also indulged in it, but women tended to dominate the form.)"<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nytimes.com_310-0"><a href="#cite_note-nytimes.com-310"><span>[</span>310<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<table class="mbox-small" style="border:1px solid #aaa;background-color:#f9f9f9;">

<div class="description" style="padding:2px 0 0 0">Carey's usage of <a href="/wiki/Melisma" title="Melisma">melisma</a> throughout the song was credited with inspiring several vocalists and performers throughout the turn of the century, and is considered to have brought the usage of the vocal technique to modern day singers and talent competitions around the world to date.</div>
</div>

</tr>
<tr>
<td class="mbox-text" colspan="2" style="line-height:1.1em"><span><i>Problems playing this file? See <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Media_help" title="Wikipedia:Media help">media help</a>.</i></span></td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>Carey is also credited for introducing R&amp;B and hip hop into mainstream pop culture, and for popularizing rap as a featuring act through her post-1995 songs. Sasha Frere-Jones, editor of <i><a href="/wiki/The_New_Yorker" title="The New Yorker">The New Yorker</a></i> commented, "It became standard for R&amp;B/hip-hop stars like <a href="/wiki/Missy_Elliott" title="Missy Elliott">Missy Elliott</a> and Beyoncé, to combine melodies with rapped verses. And young white pop stars—including <a href="/wiki/Britney_Spears" title="Britney Spears">Britney Spears</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jessica_Simpson" title="Jessica Simpson">Jessica Simpson</a>, <a href="/wiki/Christina_Aguilera" title="Christina Aguilera">Christina Aguilera</a>, and <a href="/wiki/NSYNC" title="NSYNC">'N Sync</a>—have spent much of the past ten years making pop music that is unmistakably R&amp;B." Moreover Jones concludes that "[Carey's] idea of pairing a female songbird with the leading male MCs of hip-hop changed R&amp;B and, eventually, all of pop. Although now anyone is free to use this idea, the success of <i>The Emancipation of Mimi</i> suggests that it still belongs to Carey."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-newyorker_62-6"><a href="#cite_note-newyorker-62"><span>[</span>62<span>]</span></a></sup> Judnick Mayard, writer of <i>The Fader</i>, wrote that in regarding of R&amp;B and hip hop collaboration, "The champion of this movement is Mariah Carey." Mayard also expressed that "To this day ODB and Mariah may still be the best and most random hip hop collaboration of all time", citing that due to the record "<a href="/wiki/Fantasy_(Mariah_Carey_song)" title="Fantasy (Mariah Carey song)">Fantasy</a>", "R&amp;B and Hip Hop were the best of step siblings."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-thefader.com_311-0"><a href="#cite_note-thefader.com-311"><span>[</span>311<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Kelefa Sanneh of <i>The New York Times</i> wrote, "In the mid-1990s Ms. Carey pioneered a subgenre that some people call the thug-love duet. Nowadays clean-cut pop stars are expected to collaborate with roughneck rappers, but when Ms. Carey teamed up with Ol' Dirty Bastard, of the Wu-Tang Clan, for the 1995 hit "Fantasy (Remix)", it was a surprise, and a smash."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated7_312-0"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated7-312"><span>[</span>312<span>]</span></a></sup> Aside from her pop culture and musical influence, Carey is credited for releasing a classic Christmas song called "<a href="/wiki/All_I_Want_for_Christmas_Is_You" title="All I Want for Christmas Is You">All I Want for Christmas Is You</a>".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-scotherlad_313-0"><a href="#cite_note-scotherlad-313"><span>[</span>313<span>]</span></a></sup> In a retrospective look at Carey's career, <a href="/wiki/Sasha_Frere-Jones" title="Sasha Frere-Jones">Sasha Frere-Jones</a> of <i><a href="/wiki/The_New_Yorker" title="The New Yorker">The New Yorker</a></i> said, the "charming" song was one of Carey's biggest accomplishments, calling it "one of the few worthy modern additions to the holiday canon".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-newyorker_62-7"><a href="#cite_note-newyorker-62"><span>[</span>62<span>]</span></a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/Rolling_Stone" title="Rolling Stone">Rolling Stone</a></i> ranked "All I Want for Christmas Is You" fourth on its Greatest Rock and Roll Christmas Songs list, calling it a "holiday standard."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated3_314-0"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated3-314"><span>[</span>314<span>]</span></a></sup> In a review of her <i><a href="/wiki/Greatest_Hits_(Mariah_Carey_album)" title="Greatest Hits (Mariah Carey album)">Greatest Hits</a></i> album, Devon Powers of <a href="/wiki/PopMatters" title="PopMatters">PopMatters</a> writes that "She has influenced countless female vocalists after her. At 32, she is already a living legend—even if she never sings another note."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-315"><a href="#cite_note-315"><span>[</span>315<span>]</span></a></sup> While reviewing a concert of Carey in <a href="/wiki/Sydney" title="Sydney">Sydney</a>, Elise Vout of <i><a href="/wiki/MTV_Australia" title="MTV Australia">MTV Australia</a></i> wrote that "it's not amazing choreography or high production value you're going to see, it's the larger than life personality, unique voice, and legend that is Mariah Carey."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-316"><a href="#cite_note-316"><span>[</span>316<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Personal_life">Personal life</span></h2>
<p>Carey began dating Mottola while recording <i>Music Box</i>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-shapiro5_317-0"><a href="#cite_note-shapiro5-317"><span>[</span>317<span>]</span></a></sup> and married him on June 5, 1993.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-shapiro6_106-1"><a href="#cite_note-shapiro6-106"><span>[</span>106<span>]</span></a></sup> After the release of <i>Daydream</i> and the success that followed, Carey began focusing on her personal life, which was a constant struggle at the time.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nickson38_318-0"><a href="#cite_note-nickson38-318"><span>[</span>318<span>]</span></a></sup> Carey's relationship with Mottola began to deteriorate, due to their growing creative differences in terms of her albums, as well as his controlling nature.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nickson38_318-1"><a href="#cite_note-nickson38-318"><span>[</span>318<span>]</span></a></sup> The couple divorced in 1998.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-319"><a href="#cite_note-319"><span>[</span>319<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Carey met actor and comedian <a href="/wiki/Nick_Cannon" title="Nick Cannon">Nick Cannon</a> while they shot her music video for her song "<a href="/wiki/Bye_Bye_(Mariah_Carey_song)" title="Bye Bye (Mariah Carey song)">Bye Bye</a>" on an island off the coast of <a href="/wiki/Antigua" title="Antigua">Antigua</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-success_320-0"><a href="#cite_note-success-320"><span>[</span>320<span>]</span></a></sup> On April 30, 2008, Carey married Cannon in <a href="/wiki/The_Bahamas" title="The Bahamas">The Bahamas</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated12_321-0"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated12-321"><span>[</span>321<span>]</span></a></sup> 35 weeks into her pregnancy, she gave birth to their <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fraternal_twin" title="Fraternal twin">fraternal twins</a>, Monroe and Moroccan, on April 30, 2011.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-322"><a href="#cite_note-322"><span>[</span>322<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>In August 2014, Cannon confirmed after much speculation that he and Carey had separated a few months earlier.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-323"><a href="#cite_note-323"><span>[</span>323<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Divorce_Papers_Reportedly_Filed_Between_Cannon_and_Mariah_Carey">Divorce Papers Reportedly Filed Between Cannon and Mariah Carey</span></h3>
<p>In January 2015, Hollywood and California news media sources reported the filing of divorce papers by Cannon, who apparently officially initiated divorce proceedings against Mariah Carey during their separation. However, the former couple reportedly had a <a href="/wiki/Prenuptial_agreement" title="Prenuptial agreement">prenuptial agreement</a> with a confidential clause prohibiting them from discussing certain aspects of their relationship, separation and divorce <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-324"><a href="#cite_note-324"><span>[</span>324<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Religious_.26_Christian_Faith">Religious &amp; Christian Faith</span></h3>
<p>Mariah Carey is a <a href="/wiki/Christian" title="Christian">Christian</a>. She said in 2006: "I do believe that I have been <a href="/wiki/Born_again_(Christianity)" title="Born again (Christianity)">born again</a> in a lot of ways. I think what I've changed are my priorities and my relationships with <a href="/wiki/God" title="God">God</a>. I feel the difference when I don't have my private moments to pray. ... I'm a fighter, but I learned that I'm not in charge. Whatever God wants to happen is what's going to happen. I feel like I've had endless second, third, fourth, fifth and sixth chances. It's by the grace of God I'm still here."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-325"><a href="#cite_note-325"><span>[</span>325<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Honors_and_awards">Honors and awards</span></h2>
<div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_awards_and_nominations_received_by_Mariah_Carey" title="List of awards and nominations received by Mariah Carey">List of awards and nominations received by Mariah Carey</a></div>
<p>Throughout Carey's career, she has collected many honors and awards, including the <a href="/wiki/World_Music_Awards" title="World Music Awards">World Music Awards</a>' Best Selling Female Artist of the Millennium, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Grammy" title="Grammy">Grammy</a>'s <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Best_New_Artist" title="Best New Artist">Best New Artist</a> in 1991, and <i><a href="/wiki/Billboard_(magazine)" title="Billboard (magazine)">Billboard</a>'</i>s Special Achievement Award for the Artist of the Decade during the 1990s.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-awardz_326-0"><a href="#cite_note-awardz-326"><span>[</span>326<span>]</span></a></sup> In a career spanning over 20 years, Carey has sold over 200 million records worldwide, making her <a href="/wiki/List_of_best-selling_music_artists" title="List of best-selling music artists">one of the biggest-selling artists</a> in music history.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-327"><a href="#cite_note-327"><span>[</span>327<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-328"><a href="#cite_note-328"><span>[</span>328<span>]</span></a></sup> Carey is ranked as the best-selling female artist of the <a href="/wiki/Nielsen_SoundScan" title="Nielsen SoundScan">Nielsen SoundScan</a> era, with over 52 million copies sold.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-329"><a href="#cite_note-329"><span>[</span>329<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-billboard.com_330-0"><a href="#cite_note-billboard.com-330"><span>[</span>330<span>]</span></a></sup> Possessing a <a href="/wiki/Vocal_range" title="Vocal range">five-octave vocal range</a>, Carey was ranked first in MTV and <i><a href="/wiki/Blender_(magazine)" title="Blender (magazine)">Blender</a></i> magazine's 2003 countdown of the 22 Greatest Voices in Music, and was placed second in <i>Cove</i> magazine's list of "The 100 Outstanding Pop Vocalists".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-100_Outstanding_Pop_Vocalists_275-1"><a href="#cite_note-100_Outstanding_Pop_Vocalists-275"><span>[</span>275<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-billboardbiog_331-0"><a href="#cite_note-billboardbiog-331"><span>[</span>331<span>]</span></a></sup> Aside from her voice, she has become known for her songwriting. <a href="/wiki/Yahoo!_Music" title="Yahoo! Music">Yahoo Music</a> editor Jason Ankeny wrote, "She earned frequent comparison to rivals Whitney Houston and Celine Dion, but did them both one better by composing all of her own material."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-332"><a href="#cite_note-332"><span>[</span>332<span>]</span></a></sup> According to <i>Billboard</i> magazine, she was the most successful artist of the 1990s in the United States.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEShapiro2001145_333-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEShapiro2001145-333"><span>[</span>333<span>]</span></a></sup> At the 2000 <a href="/wiki/World_Music_Awards" title="World Music Awards">World Music Awards</a>, Carey was given a Legend Award for being the "best-selling female pop artist of the millennium", as well as the "Best-selling artist of the 90s" in the United States, after releasing a series of albums of multiplatinum status in Asia and Europe, such as <i><a href="/wiki/Music_Box_(Mariah_Carey_album)" title="Music Box (Mariah Carey album)">Music Box</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Number_1%27s_(Mariah_Carey_album)" title="Number 1's (Mariah Carey album)">Number 1's</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-billboardbiog_331-1"><a href="#cite_note-billboardbiog-331"><span>[</span>331<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-334"><a href="#cite_note-334"><span>[</span>334<span>]</span></a></sup> She is also a recipient of the <a href="/wiki/Chopard_Diamond_award" title="Chopard Diamond award">Chopard Diamond award</a> in 2003, recognizing sales of over 100 million albums worldwide.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NME_Artists_-_Mariah_Carey_335-0"><a href="#cite_note-NME_Artists_-_Mariah_Carey-335"><span>[</span>335<span>]</span></a></sup> Additionally, the <a href="/wiki/Recording_Industry_Association_of_America" title="Recording Industry Association of America">Recording Industry Association of America</a> (RIAA) lists Carey as the third-best-selling female artist, with shipments of over 63 million units in the US.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-riaa.com_336-0"><a href="#cite_note-riaa.com-336"><span>[</span>336<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Mariah_Marks_Milestone_337-0"><a href="#cite_note-Mariah_Marks_Milestone-337"><span>[</span>337<span>]</span></a></sup> In Japan, Carey has the top four highest-selling albums of all time by a non-Asian artist.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-338"><a href="#cite_note-338"><span>[</span>338<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Carey has spent 79 weeks at the number-one position on <a href="/wiki/Billboard_Hot_100" title="Billboard Hot 100"><i>Billboard</i> Hot 100</a>, the greatest number for any artist in US chart history.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-billboard1_339-0"><a href="#cite_note-billboard1-339"><span>[</span>339<span>]</span></a></sup> On that same chart, she has accumulated 18 number-one singles, the most for any solo artist (and second after <a href="/wiki/The_Beatles" title="The Beatles">The Beatles</a>).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hiscock_340-0"><a href="#cite_note-Hiscock-340"><span>[</span>340<span>]</span></a></sup> In 1994, Carey released her holiday album <i><a href="/wiki/Merry_Christmas_(Mariah_Carey_album)" title="Merry Christmas (Mariah Carey album)">Merry Christmas</a></i> has sold over 15 million copies worldwide, and is the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Best-selling_Christmas/holiday_albums_in_the_United_States" title="Best-selling Christmas/holiday albums in the United States">best-selling Christmas album</a> of all time.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mimisales2_63-2"><a href="#cite_note-mimisales2-63"><span>[</span>63<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-national_64-1"><a href="#cite_note-national-64"><span>[</span>64<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sasha_341-0"><a href="#cite_note-sasha-341"><span>[</span>341<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-independent_342-0"><a href="#cite_note-independent-342"><span>[</span>342<span>]</span></a></sup> It also produced the successful single "<a href="/wiki/All_I_Want_for_Christmas_Is_You" title="All I Want for Christmas Is You">All I Want for Christmas Is You</a>", which became the only holiday song and <a href="/wiki/Ringtone" title="Ringtone">ringtone</a> to reach multi-platinum status in the US.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-343"><a href="#cite_note-343"><span>[</span>343<span>]</span></a></sup> In Japan, <i>Number 1's</i> has sold over 3,250,000 copies and is the <a href="/wiki/List_of_best-selling_albums_in_Japan" title="List of best-selling albums in Japan">best-selling album of all time in Japan</a> by a non-Asian artist.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Mariah_Carey_.231.27s_344-0"><a href="#cite_note-Mariah_Carey_.231.27s-344"><span>[</span>344<span>]</span></a></sup> Her hit single "<a href="/wiki/One_Sweet_Day" title="One Sweet Day">One Sweet Day</a>", which featured <a href="/wiki/Boyz_II_Men" title="Boyz II Men">Boyz II Men</a>, spent sixteen consecutive weeks at the top of <i>Billboard</i> '​s Hot 100 chart in 1996, setting the record for the <a href="/wiki/List_of_Billboard_Hot_100_chart_achievements_and_milestones" title="List of Billboard Hot 100 chart achievements and milestones">most weeks atop the Hot 100 chart in history</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-billboard.com_330-1"><a href="#cite_note-billboard.com-330"><span>[</span>330<span>]</span></a></sup> After Carey's success in Asia with <i>Merry Christmas</i>, <i>Billboard</i> estimated Carey as the all-time best-selling international artist in Japan.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lichtman_345-0"><a href="#cite_note-Lichtman-345"><span>[</span>345<span>]</span></a></sup> In 2008, <i>Billboard</i> listed "We Belong Together" ninth on The <a href="/wiki/Billboard_Hot_100_50th_Anniversary_Charts" title="Billboard Hot 100 50th Anniversary Charts">Billboard Hot 100 All-Time Top Songs</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated8_346-0"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated8-346"><span>[</span>346<span>]</span></a></sup> and second on Top Billboard Hot 100 R&amp;B/Hip-Hop Songs.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-yahoosales2_347-0"><a href="#cite_note-yahoosales2-347"><span>[</span>347<span>]</span></a></sup> The song was also declared the most popular song of the 2000s decade by <i>Billboard</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-decade_150-1"><a href="#cite_note-decade-150"><span>[</span>150<span>]</span></a></sup> In 2009, Carey's cover of <a href="/wiki/Foreigner_(band)" title="Foreigner (band)">Foreigner</a>'s song "<a href="/wiki/I_Want_to_Know_What_Love_Is" title="I Want to Know What Love Is">I Want to Know What Love Is</a>" became the longest-running number-one song in Brazilian singles chart history, spending 27 consecutive weeks at number-one.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-348"><a href="#cite_note-348"><span>[</span>348<span>]</span></a></sup> Additionally, Carey has had three songs debut at number-one on the <i>Billboard</i> Hot 100: "<a href="/wiki/Fantasy_(Mariah_Carey_song)" title="Fantasy (Mariah Carey song)">Fantasy</a>", "<a href="/wiki/One_Sweet_Day" title="One Sweet Day">One Sweet Day</a>" and "<a href="/wiki/Honey_(Mariah_Carey_song)" title="Honey (Mariah Carey song)">Honey</a>", making her the artist with the most number-one debuts in the chart's 52-year history.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-349"><a href="#cite_note-349"><span>[</span>349<span>]</span></a></sup> Also, she is the first female artist to debut at number 1 in the U.S. with "<a href="/wiki/Fantasy_(Mariah_Carey_song)" title="Fantasy (Mariah Carey song)">Fantasy</a>".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-billboardbiog_331-2"><a href="#cite_note-billboardbiog-331"><span>[</span>331<span>]</span></a></sup> In 2010, Carey's 13th album and second Christmas album, <i><a href="/wiki/Merry_Christmas_II_You" title="Merry Christmas II You">Merry Christmas II You</a></i>, debuted at No.1 on the <a href="/wiki/Top_R%26B/Hip-Hop_Albums" title="Top R&amp;B/Hip-Hop Albums">R&amp;B/Hip-Hop Albums</a> chart, making it only the second Christmas album to top that chart. On November 19, 2010, <i>Billboard</i> magazine named Carey in their "Top 50 R&amp;B/Hip-Hop Artists of the Past 25 Years" chart at number four.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-350"><a href="#cite_note-350"><span>[</span>350<span>]</span></a></sup> In 2012, Carey was ranked second on <a href="/wiki/VH1" title="VH1">VH1</a>'s list of the "100 Greatest Women in Music".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-351"><a href="#cite_note-351"><span>[</span>351<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
